# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Ingress v1beta1 to v1 Migration

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement Ingress API handling for both v1beta1 and v1: the conversion functions between versions, the validation changes (pathType became required), and the storage version migration logic.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json

}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I have completed a comprehensive analysis of the Kubernetes Ingress API handling for v1beta1 to v1 migration. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

I've identified **21 relevant Go source files** in the kubernetes/kubernetes v1.32.0 repository that implement Ingress API handling for both v1beta1 and v1, including:

### Main Components:

1. **Conversion Functions**: 
   - Manual conversions in `pkg/apis/networking/v1beta1/conversion.go` handle the backend structure migration (ServiceName/ServicePort → Service/Port)
   - Auto-generated conversions in both v1 and v1beta1 zz_generated.conversion.go files handle HTTPIngressPath and Ingress conversions

2. **Validation Changes**:
   - `pkg/apis/networking/validation/validation.go` enforces PathType requirement - v1 requires PathType to be specified, while v1beta1 allows it to be optional

3. **Defaults**:
   - `pkg/apis/networking/v1beta1/defaults.go` sets default PathType to `ImplementationSpecific` for v1beta1
   - `pkg/apis/networking/v1/defaults.go` has no defaults - PathType must be explicit in v1

4. **Type Definitions**:
   - v1 HTTPIngressPath has PathType as required
   - v1beta1 HTTPIngressPath has PathType as optional with default behavior

5. **Storage and Strategy**:
   - Strategy implementation in `pkg/registry/networking/ingress/strategy.go` validates using the networking validation functions
   - Supports all three versions: extensions/v1beta1, networking.k8s.io/v1beta1, and networking.k8s.io/v1

The answer has been written to `/workspace/answer.json` with detailed file listings, key symbols, conversion chain, and a comprehensive narrative explanation.

If multiple matching paths exist in an Ingress spec, the\n461: \t// longest matching path is given priority.\n462: \t// Examples:\n463: \t// - /foo/bar does not match requests to /foo/barbaz\n464: \t// - /foo/bar matches request to /foo/bar and /foo/bar/baz\n465: \t// - /foo and /foo/ both match requests to /foo and /foo/. If both paths are\n466: \t//   present in an Ingress spec, the longest matching path (/foo/) is given\n467: \t//   priority.\n468: \tPathTypePrefix = PathType(\"Prefix\")\n469: \n470: \t// PathTypeImplementationSpecific matching is up to the IngressClass.\n471: \t// Implementations can treat this as a separate PathType or treat it\n472: \t// identically to Prefix or Exact path types.\n473: \tPathTypeImplementationSpecific = PathType(\"ImplementationSpecific\")\n474: )\n475: \n476: // HTTPIngressPath associates a path with a backend. Incoming urls matching the\n477: // path are forwarded to the backend.\n478: type HTTPIngressPath struct {\n479: \t// path is matched against the path of an incoming request. Currently it can\n480: \t// contain characters disallowed from the conventional \"path\" part of a URL\n481: \t// as defined by RFC 3986. Paths must begin with a '/' and must be present\n482: \t// when using PathType with value \"Exact\" or \"Prefix\".\n483: \t// +optional\n484: \tPath string `json:\"path,omitempty\" protobuf:\"bytes,1,opt,name=path\"`\n485: \n486: \t// pathType determines the interpretation of the path matching. PathType can\n487: \t// be one of the following values:\n488: \t// * Exact: Matches the URL path exactly.\n489: \t// * Prefix: Matches based on a URL path prefix split by '/'. Matching is\n490: \t//   done on a path element by element basis. A path element refers is the\n491: \t//   list of labels in the path split by the '/' separator. A request is a\n492: \t//   match for path p if every p is an element-wise prefix of p of the\n493: \t//   request path. Note that if the last element of the path is a substring\n494: \t//   of the last element in request path, it is not a match (e.g. /foo/bar\n495: \t//   matches /foo/bar/baz, but does not match /foo/barbaz).\n496: \t// * ImplementationSpecific: Interpretation of the Path matching is up to\n497: \t//   the IngressClass. Implementations can treat this as a separate PathType\n498: \t//   or treat it identically to Prefix or Exact path types.\n499: \t// Implementations are required to support all path types.\n500: \tPathType *PathType `json:\"pathType\" protobuf:\"bytes,3,opt,name=pathType\"`\n501: \n502: \t// backend defines the referenced service endpoint to which the traffic\n503: \t// will be forwarded to.\n504: \tBackend IngressBackend `json:\"backend\" protobuf:\"bytes,2,opt,name=backend\"`\n505: }\n506: \n507: // IngressBackend describes all endpoints for a given service and port.\n508: type IngressBackend struct {\n509: \t// service references a service as a backend.\n510: \t// This is a mutually exclusive setting with \"Resource\".\n511: \t// +optional\n512: \tService *IngressServiceBackend `json:\"service,omitempty\" protobuf:\"bytes,4,opt,name=service\"`\n513: \n514: \t// resource is an ObjectRef to another Kubernetes resource in the namespace\n515: \t// of the Ingress object.
